To Our Advertisers:
We extend our gratitude, not only for making
this publication possible, but also for the support
you lend to our many activities. We urge our
members to reciprocate with their patronage.
About the Cover:
Dedicating this Yearbook to Raymond
Cohen is especially fitting, for he has been
involved with the Center Yearbook in a variety
of roles for some 50 years. During that time,
he created or consulted on almost half of the
covers, served on the advisory committee,
produced ads and layouts, and was editor of
the award-winning Centennial issue.
When informed by the Board of this
honor, Raymond was overwhelmed, but true
to his volunteer spirit, offered to do the cover
of this issue.
In a play on Norman Rockwell, Raymond
has created a drawing that crystallizes past and
present in a dejavu experience. In his youth and
in his prime, Raymond has not wavered from
his love of Judaism as expressed through art,
music and devotion to the synagogue. With
humor and candor, Raymond reveals that he
has matured but is still vibrant and vital, ever
ready to apply his talents in service to the
Jacksonville Jewish Center.

===== PAGE 5 =====
A Tribute to Raymond Cohen
for his lifelong contributions of time and talent in service to our synagogue
Art, music and love of Judaism have always
been intertwined in the life of Raymond Cohen, and
he has never hesitated to share his talents with
enthusiasm and grace. He is a longtime friend to
many in our congregation, and exemplifies the best
that the Jacksonville Jewish Center has to offer.
Raymond’s personal history is tightly woven
into the history of this congregation. His life spans
the generations and is a bridge to the future.
Bom in Jacksonville on
January 4, 1921, Raymond
was the youngest of the four
children of Ida and Joseph
Cohen. The couple, like other
Pusheloters, helped start this
congregation and were
founding members of B’nai
Israel, as our synagogue was
then named.
Jewish education was especially precious to
Raymond’s mother, whose own father had been a
Yeshiva student in Lithuania. Naturally, Eddie, Macy,
Bessie and Raymond were enrolled in Hebrew
school at the synagogue on Jefferson and Duval.
Raymond would later become Bar Mitzvah on the
pulpit of the new Jacksonville
Jewish Center at 3rd and
Silver. It was there, that he
learned to daven with devotion
and began to develop his
unparalleled hazzanuut.
As a teen in the 1930s,
Raymond joined one of the
youth groups that were bringing
the spirit of Zionism to
communities like ours. In
Rothchild Young Judea,
Raymond experienced the
satisfaction of volunteering for Jewish causes, that
would carry over into adulthood.
i
===== PAGE 6 =====
From childhood, Raymond
displayed a gifted vocal talent. A
seasoned junior Cantor at 13, he
joined the adult choir and began nearly
70 years as featured soloist in the
Center’s Friday night, holiday and
concert choirs. At 82 years old, his
singing is still an inspirational highlight
of our High Holiday services.
On March 12, 1939 at age 18,
Raymond made his stage debut in the original operetta
called “The Wedding.” It was touted as the “most
elaborate and most beautiful [musical] ever given in
Jacksonville by the Jewish community.” The love story
had 6 scenes and twenty pieces of music based on Jewish
folk songs and fragments of folklife in Eastern Europe.
Raymond’s magnificent tenor voice would win him a
scholarship to Stetson University.
r to l: Isidor Setzer, Irving Slott, May Schweitzer, Meyer Leibovitz,
Sylvia Price, Morris Nimovitz, Raymond Cohen, Leo Moskovitz,
Mrs. Abraham Prattler, Melvin Margol.
On a parallel course with his musical development,
Raymond’s artistic talents came to the forefront. He was
awarded a scholarship to the Ringling School of Art,
attended the University of Florida, the Long School of
Art and later, New York University.
World War II interrupted Raymond’s education, but
the skills he had already acquired allowed him to rise
above the ordinary tasks of
a foot-soldier. He was
assigned to the U.S. Army
Printing Plant in Orlando.
Among other things, he
designed recruitment posters
and materials for the
Officer’s Club. Raymond
was chosen to be part of a
drafting team that worked on
plans for air strips, as well as
the Norden bombsite.
Raymond never strayed from his Jewish roots.
Soon he became the Cantor for Friday night Services on
the base. He also designed a portable Aron Kodesh that
was used by Jewish chaplains in the field.
After one Shabbat evening Service, Raymond was
introduced to a cute WAAC from New York, named
Dorothy Berger. It was love at
first sight and 6 months later the
couple was married by the base
chaplain. They have been making
beautiful music together ever
since. This November, Dorothy
and Raymond will celebrate their
60th wedding anniversary.
Upon his honorable discharge, Raymond returned
to Jacksonville to begin civilian life, as a young husband
and new father to son, Jerry. In time there would be two
daughters, Peggy and Karen.
Raymond now pursued his passion for art, as a
profession, in the advertising department of Cohen
Brother’s, where he became Advertising and Sales
Promotion Manager. At the request of his brothers,
Raymond opened and managed the successful Toy Fair
store in San Marco, but soon returned to advertising.
Over the next three decades, he built the Raymond Cohen
Advertising Agency into an award-winning, regional firm.
All the while, Raymond continued to sing. In 1948,
Cantor Abraham Marton formed the first mixed chorus
at the Jacksonville Jewish Center. He introduced liturgical
and popular Jewish music written by world-famous
composers. Raymond became his star male vocalist and
performed stirring solos in Services, as well as in concert
with the Choral Society. The choir even performed on
television.
A clipping from the Times Union shows (r to l) accompanist Jimmy
Crosland, Cantor Marton, Reba Torn, Leo Moskovitz, Raymond
Cohen and Celia Bressler rehearsing for a concert in 1950.
===== PAGE 7 =====
In the 1950s and 60s, a
wedding at the Center wasn’t
complete unless Raymond
Cohen sang. It was a present to
the bride that he enjoyed as
much as the guests. In addition
to friends and congregants,
Raymond sang at all the
weddings of his children. He was even invited to perform
at the U.S. Senate Dining room for the wedding reception
of Senator George McGovern’s daughter.
Though he has been cast in
many roles in community plays
and operas, Raymond has always
been a willing participant in our
home-grown theatrical productions
for holidays, Center variety shows
and special events.
Raymond has a terrific sense of humor, but he is
very serious about his artistic contributions to the Center.
He has produced numerous brochures and programs, as
well as the creative service booklet that was used for
many years on the second day of Rosh Hashanah. He
was also a member of the sanctuary design committee.
Raymond designed the
Center Centennial logo
used on printed pieces, a
commemorative pin and a
ceremonial menorah, as well
as the Yom HaMorim torch
representing 100 years of
Education at the Center.
Raymond’s devotion to the Center Yearbook has
been extensive and on-going since the early 50s. Although
many people are familiar with his design work, Raymond’s
fine drawings and paintings of religious and secular
subjects grace the walls of many congregants’ homes.
Several have been reproduced on covers of the Yearbook.
In addition, Raymond has worked behind the scenes as a
print advisor, ad and layout artist, and editor. The Center
Yearbook staff is extremely proud to honor Raymond
and express their appreciation for all his efforts. He has
added immeasurably to the success of the publication.
Behind every great man their is a great woman.
Dorothy has been Raymond’s soulmate, partner, critic,
advisor and biggest fan. Together they have created a
meaningful Jewish life for themselves and their children
based on family traditions. Holiday observance, Jewish
education, tzedakah, ethical behavior, respect for the
elderly, love of the synagogue and involvement in the
community were taught to their children by example.
Both Jerry and Peggy (Organes) began their formal
education in the Center’s Kindergarten, Hebrew and
Sunday Schools. There was no double standard, each
was expected to study for Bar and Bat Mitzvah.
Raymond supervised the training at home, spending
countless hours listening to haftarahs and prayers. He is
planning to duplicate his own Bar Mitzvah next January
at age 83.
Daughter, Karen (Morse), was enrolled in the first
class of the Center’s Foundation School. Later all of the
Jacksonville grandchildren would receive a Solomon
Schechter education.
Family is everything to Raymond. Growing up at
the Center, most everyone was his family. The term
“Center Family” was real. More than that, was the deep
relationship he had with his mother and brother, Macy.
Taking the children to their
grandmother’s house for Shabbat
and holidays became a ritual
Raymond and Dot passed down to
their own grandchildren. David and
Rachel Organes were literally
taught the Kiddush as babes in
arms. Now Ben, Maci and Trudy
Morse take turns leading each
week. Gainesville granddaughter,
Marsha Cohen davens in her shul.
And of course the singing at Seders is rich with harmony,
when the Cohen clan gathers from all over.
After Macy died, Raymond said Kaddish at each
minyan, joined by son-in-law, Ken. They both became
regulars and were minyan captains for a number of years.
Raymond still davens on Monday mornings, with son-
in-law, Todd, and grandson, Ben in attendance.
Raymond continues to lead an admirable life and
has received the accolades of our congregation, including
that of Hatan Torah. But he considers his biggest success
to be in the lives of his children and grandchildren.
Following his lead, they sing in the choir, take leadership
roles in the congregation, plan and participate in synagogue
celebrations, and even work on the Yearbook.
Mazel Tov to Raymond, Dorothy and their family
on this well-deserved honor. Through your example,
others will be inspired to contribute their time and talent
to the Jacksonville Jewish Center, keeping our congregation
vibrant for generations to come.
If there’s a Purim speil,
Raymond will be in it. One his
favorite roles was Mordechai, in “Esther and the King of
Shushan,” a costume
musical directed by
Marilyn Garber. He has
been the emcee for a
string of hilarious, adult,
Shushan Purim dinners.
He even played, what
else, the “cantor” in this
year’s Purim play.
iii

A Expression of Esteem for Raymond Cohen
from Rabbi Stephen and Judy Grundfast and Family
As the great King David was about to leave
this earth, the Tanach records his final words, in
the book of Second Samuel, chapter 23, “The
spirit of the Lord spoke to me, and His word
was in my tongue.”
David was called N'eem zemirot Yisraeyl,
the sweet singer of Israel, for through his music
and singing he was able to become ever closer
to God and serve the Almighty with all his soul
and all his might.
A great honor has been bestowed upon our
own sweet singer of Israel, Raymond Cohen.
For many years his voice has filled the hearts of
our congregants with a beautiful voice that has
touched and transformed our souls. Raymond
speaks to God as he lifts his voice in song with
great kavanah, spirit.
The Talmud states, “...the essential in the
music of the (ancient) Sanctuary was the singing
with the mouth, the instrument music being just
for sweetening the sound.” Raymond is essential
to the Jacksonville Jewish Center for he sweetens
our worship each and every time he shares his
sacred talent with us, be that on the Yamim
Noraim, Selichot night or at special
congregational occasions.
But even more important than his
beautiful singing voice is Raymonds sweetness
as a human being. Raymond is a gutte neshamah,
a good soul, with a kind word for everyone he
meets. His smile is infectious and we all should
emulate his gentleness and compassion for
others.
There is a lesson to be learned from the
two seas in the Land of Israel. The Jordan River
feeds into the seas with sparkling water from
the hills above. The first sea is fresh with a
multitude of fish in its waters and lush vegetation
on its banks. The Jordan River continues to flow
southward into another sea, but there are no
fish to be found and its banks are barren.
What makes this mighty difference
between these two seas? It is not the Jordan
River. It empties the same good water into both.
This is the difference:
The Sea of Galilee receives but does not
keep the Jordan. For every drop that flows into
it, another drop flows out. The giving and
receiving go on in equal measure.
The other sea is much different. It hoards
its incoming water with great jealousy. It has no
such generosity as the first sea. Every drop it
acquires it keeps.
The Sea of Galilee gives and lives. The other
sea cannot sustain life. It is called the Dead Sea.
There are two kinds of seas in the Land of
Israel, and there are two kinds of people in the
world. Raymond Cohen is our Sea of Galilee.
He gives with great joy to all who know and
love him. And each of us receives the great
benefit of his sweetness.
We hope and pray that God grant
Raymond many more years of life and song so
that he can share his special and holy talents with
us all. May he truly go from strength to strength.
With fondest regards,
Rabbi Stephen and Judy Grundfast and Family

In Appreciation of Raymond Cohen
From Rabbi S’ Inge Gaffney
In Exodus 25, the Torah describes God’s
command to Moses to build a Tabernacle with all the
requisite furnishings —an Ark to house the tablets with
the inscribed Ten Commandments; the Menorah, the
Altars; a Table for Showbread, etc. Moses is,
understandably, overwhelmed. His greatest
responsibility is to lead the people of Israel through
the wilderness to the Promised Land. He lacks the
time, the skills, as well as the aesthetic wherewithal to
undertake a project as significant as fashioning a
Tabernacle.
But God has commanded - “Let them make me
a sanctuary so that I may dwell within them”. (Exodus
25:8)
Sensing Moses’ dilemma, God offers - “see I have
singled out to assist you, Bezalel. I have endowed him
with Divine Spirit, with aesthetic skill and knowledge
in every craft. (Exodus 31: 3-5) Commentators explain
the words “singled out” to signify Bezalel’s unique and
exemplary reputation, because he used his talent and
skill For the most worthy of purposes - creating a
sanctuary where God’s presence would be found.
Moses is relieved. A sanctuary, a place of holiness
requires more than the efforts of one man, one leader -
even a Moses -but the assistance and support of those
who are filled with skill and talent and the spirit of
God.
For the twenty-nine years of my association with
the Jacksonville Jewish Center my Bezalel was Raymond
Cohen. His service to the Center is of even longer
duration - a total of sixty-nine years. Blessed with
artistic skill and an aesthetic sense, Raymond willingly
and generously shared his talent, sensitivity and
devotion with the Center.
As titular leader of the Center Chorale Society
for about twenty years, Raymond’s beautiful tenor voice
moved countless worshippers with his renditions of
u’v’SHOFAR GADOL YI-TA-KA of the u’n’TANEH TOKEF
prayer. Can anyone forget his rendering of ZAHARTI
lach of the High Holiday Musaf Service?
Raymond’s voice in concert with other choir
voices enhanced our holiday services, late Friday evening
services, Confirmation services, etc. Raymond
volunteered his talent on other occasions - Shushan
Purim, Center Raffles, evenings that featured talent
programs, Israel Bond programs and for many occasions
throughout the year.
It was not only with his voice that Raymond
moved us. His artistic skills were put to use in service
of Center Yearbook covers, advertising campaigns for
building fund efforts; when we celebrated the 100th
anniversary of the founding of the Center and for many
other comparable occasions.
Equally gratifying to me were the ten years in
which Raymond served as a Monday morning minyan
captain. Countless people who needed the comforting
support of a minyan when they were saying Kaddish
were assured that a minyan would be available because
of Raymond’s devotion. His own “menschlikheit” helps
to explain his being “singled out” - as he is this year;
his exemplary reputation as the Bezalel of the
Jacksonville Jewish Center.
The Center has always been a second home to
Raymond and his ayshet ci-layil —his “Woman of Valor”
-his beloved Dot. How gratified they are to experience
their children and grandchildren joining the Center
Choir, adding their own voices to the Service of God,
making for a perfect harmony —not only of voices -
but of a beautiful family harmony, as well. Their
children Peggy and Ken, Karen and Todd and their
grandchildren David, Rachel, Ben, Maci and Trudy
nave looked to the Center as a place in which to flourish
Jewishly. Their children Jerry and Sherry and
granddaughter Marsha, when visiting from Gainesville,
recognize that Raymond and Dot enjoy the love and
respect of so many Center friends. May their lives
continue to be rich with happiness -as they have
enriched our lives. May they celebrate many happy
occasions with their entire family including their
grandchildren Tavi and Grant, Michael and Michelle,
and great grandchildren Shannon, Evan and Matthew.
Inge and I join all of our Center friends in wishing
Raymond and Dot a long and healthy life, filled with
joy and happiness and naches and the satisfaction that
comes in the knowledge that they have helped to create
a Tabernacle —a sanctuary -our beloved Jacksonville
Jewish Center.
Best wishes for a healthy and
meaningful Shanah Tovah to all.
— Rabbi & Inge Gaffney

Honoring Raymond Cohen
for his lifelong contributions of time and talent in service to our synagogue
Congratulations Papa
For generations we have heard Ema say, “Be quiet, your father/
your grandfather/your great-grandfather is singing!”
It is hard to remember a time at the Center when you weren’t
the featured soloist, performing with the family in a play, singing at
a wedding, or leading services. You have become so much a part of
what the Center is, that it could never be the same without you.
To paraphrase Kohelet, “Rabbi’s have come and gone, and the
Cantor also changes, but it appears that the indelible imprint of
your spirit will abide in our hearts and souls forever.”
This is your legacy. Yasher koach.
Jerry & Sherry Marsha
Michelle, Mike & Matthew Tavi, Grant, Shannon & Evan

===== PAGE 12 =====
Honoring Raymond Cohen
for his lifelong contributions of time and talent in service to our synagogue
Jacksonville Jewish Center Groundbreaking, December 20, 1987
“And all thy children shall be taught the Lord, and great shall be the peace of thy
children.” - Isaiah. Rabbi Hanina said of that passage, “Read not banayich, thy
children, but bonayich, thy builders, for the children are the builders of our future.”
Dad, you have built a rich life, for yourself and your family, based on the wisdom
of Judaism and a heartfelt calling to use your talents in service to our congregation.
You taught us by your example and we have tried to teach our children, in turn.
The Torah tells us that when the Sanctuary was to be built, God “called” the artist
and filled him with wisdom, understanding and knowledge that his works might
inspire and uplift others.
Dad, you have been blessed with an exceptional talent, both for the visual arts and
for music, which you used to fashion a fulfilling creative career and rewarding vocal
avocation. But by answering the call, using your gifts for the benefit of the synagogue,
you have achieved far greater success — you are an inspiration. “The highest artist,
in the eyes of Jewish teachers of all generations, is not the master of self-expression
but of self-control — he who fashions himself into a sanctuary.” You are that artist.
Dad, you and Mom have our love, our respect and our gratitude, always,
Peggy, Ken, David and Rachel

A Prayer for the New Year
Dear God,
Creator and Sustainer of all, who has breathed the spirit of life into dust, we the
children of the people of Israel, assembled in holy congregations this year on the holy
days of Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, bend our heads before you in thankfulness
and deep gratitude for all the favors and kindnesses, that you have shown in mercy to
us during the past year that is now passing into eternity.
In humbleness and silence, do we accept all the woes and afflictions that You, in
your wisdom and mercy, permitted to befall us.
We pray to you, O Lord, to bestow upon us, and upon all your children, for this
coming year, from the multitude of bounties, to the gift of life, to have a healthy
existence, to the full use of all the faculties of body and mind. Purify the hearts and
guide the minds of people so that your gift of life may not be put to vain and foolish
use. May this coming year of 5764 contribute towards the realization in the life of
humankind of the vision of the Prophets, the vision so beautifully formulated in our
prayer to you on this day, “Rule Thou alone, O Lord, over all Thy creatures.”
It is to strive to bring glory to your name, to help to establish justice and peace
among people, to aid in the restoration of Israel, their people, to the soil you have
ordained for it from old, to strive to implant in the hearts of our children love and
knowledge of the Torah and the Jewish faith, that we pray, O Lord, “Remember us
unto life, O King! Thou who delights in life, and write us in the book of life for Thy
sake, O God of life.”
Amen
To all our friends, a year of peace and good health, and to children everywhere, we pledge our efforts to improve the world.
East Coast Fruit Co., Inc.
Goldie Portnoy
Jerry & Barbara Portnoy and Family Michael & Andrea Portnoy and Family
Richard & Rhonda Passink and Family
with the hope that it will nurture some reflections on the High Holidays. It is presented with wishes for a healthy, happy New Year.

===== PAGE 25 =====
A Message from Rabbi Grundfast
Teshuvah - Our Journey Towards Wholeness
The Yamim Noraim, High Holy Days,
beckon us to alter our lives and become
better Jews and human beings, in our fast
moving and highly technological society, we
sometimes leave little space or occasion for
personal reflection and spiritual growth.
Many of us today feel as if we have become
exiled from God’s holy presence by our
mistakes, unfulfilled obligations and missed
opportunities.
Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur should
make us tremble as we stand not only in
God’s judgment, but perhaps even more importantly, in
judgment of ourselves. The Talmud speaks of three books
that are opened at this time of year, namely, a book for the
thoroughly righteous; one for the thoroughly wicked and a
third one for all the intermediate. (Talmud, Rosh Hashanah
16b). According to this rabbinic legend, God scrutinizes our
actions and our names are thus inscribed in one of those
heavenly ledgers.
For me, this well-known Talmudic passage is a
metaphor for the hard and arduous task of self-judgment. We
ourselves are endowed with the power and ability to “move”
God’s hand towards a year of goodness, by how we act and by
how much kindness we exhibit to those around us. The
majority of us are presently in the intermediate book, for we
are “the middle of the road sinners.” The ten-day time period
between the beginning of Rosh Hashanah and the sounding
of the shofar at the conclusion of Yom Kippur provides us
with a final possibility to make a life or death difference in
the world.
it was once written that Teshuvah, repentance, sweetens
our journey towards wholeness. The self-realization that we
can be better people is one of the great teachings that must
be gleaned from our High Holy Days. It is a new year, and it
is now time to make a new start. Our journey towards
wholeness and spiritual healing will not happen automatically.
There is no magic formula for personal
change, just the ability to see ourselves in a
new light. We must do the hard and arduous
work on our own.
The month of Elul, which precedes the
holiday of Rosh Hashanah, is viewed in our
tradition as an especially important time for
Teshuvah and personal introspection. In
Gematria the word “Elul” has the numerical
equivalent of the Hebrew word binah, that
means understanding. The meaning is
simple: only through understanding can
Teshuvah ever become a living reality in our lives. As it is
stated by the prophet Isaiah (6:10), “And understanding with
their heart, return and be healed.”
Rabbi Israel Salanter, a popular 19th century sage
from Lithuania, was the founder of the Musar movement.
Musar, a moral school of thought and action teaches that
ethical behavior is to be performed and perfected in the
spirit of Halacha, Jewish law. He was a great and
distinguished teacher and preacher who taught the following
lesson, which I believe holds great meaning and significance
for us in today’s challenging world.
He taught that each person has two eyes for a reason.
With one eye, we look at our neighbors, fastening our gaze
on their goodness, excellence, and most desirable qualities,
while refraining from criticism, slander and gossip. With
the other eye, we turn inward to see our own weaknesses,
imperfections so we can correct them.
As the prophet Ezekiel wrote, “Cast away from
yourselves all your transgressions, and create within
yourselves a new heart and a new spirit.” (Ezekiel 18: 31)
May we see the New Year with clear eyes and pure
hearts so that we can move ever closer to the Divine One,
and that our year will be blessed with good health and moral
fortitude.
Allow me to take this opportunity to wish
Raymond Cohen a hearty Mazal Tov. He is most deserving
of having the yearbook dedicated in his honor as we celebrate
and recognize his many years of dedicated service to the
Jacksonville Jewish Center and to the Jewish People. May
God continue sending His blessings upon Raymond, a man
with a gutte neshamah.
On behalf of my wife, Judy and children, Rachel and
Joe, may I wish each of you a Shanah Tovah u’Metukah—a
good and a sweet new year.
— Rabbi Stephen Grundfast
Rabbi Stephen Grundfast

Administration
Executive Director’s Message
One day, during this past
summer, the phone rang from a
Center member who had not been
around in quite some time. He asked
for an appointment and said it was
rather important.
When he arrived at the Center
a few hours later he seemed to have
a lot on his mind. He proceeded to
say that it had been a longtime since
he stepped foot in the building, but
had attended minyan earlier in the
week to observe a yarzheit.
“I just want you to know,” he said, “that even
though you haven’t seen me here in sometime, I
am very grateful to the Jacksonville Jewish Center
because I know the shul will always be here when I
need it.”
What a warm thought! The member then
proceeded to say he now had some free time on his
hands and would like to volunteer. “Is there anything
you need?” He was immediately given a project,
which he completed with great pride.
Who knows what ignited the spark that
reconnected this long-standing member with the
Jacksonville Jewish Center? But the lesson is clear.
The Center will always be here when you need it.
Whether it’s a yarzheit, a simcha, a holiday
observance or an educational opportunity, the
Center remains steadfastly committed to serving its
members seven days a week, 365 days a year.
This commitment is made possible through
the dedication of our staff, teachers, outstanding
lay leadership and dedicated volunteers.
Our volunteers, in particular,
play a critical role in the life of our
congregation. From youth advisors
and minyan captains, to Shabbat
greeters, PTA presidents, committee
chairman, statement stuffers,
fundraisers and other volunteers, the
opportunities are endless.
That is why this gentleman’s
question, “Is there anything you
need?” resonates. The Center will
always be here when you need it, but
“yes” we need your help as well. Volunteer to serve
the Center in some capacity. Offer your assistance
to the office, a youth group, a minyan, a school
program, or a synagogue committee. Call us and ask,
“Is there anything you need?” We will be happy to
match your talents and time with our needs.
As we approach the New Year 5764,1 want to
personally express my gratitude to the staff and
membership of the Jacksonville Jewish Center for
making our synagogue so unique. We enter the New
Year with great hope and optimism for the future of
Jewish life in Jacksonville and beyond.
I would also like to express my deepest
appreciation to Raymond Cohen, our Yearbook
honoree, who embodies the spirit of volunteerism.
Whether its leading the Center Choral Society,
designing award winning covers for our Yearbook or
serving as a Monday morning minyan captain,
Raymond has touched the life of this congregation
for well over a half a century. Todah rabah,
Raymond, and continued years of good health
and happiness for you, Dorothy and your entire
family.
On behalf of my family, Edith, Sam and Max,
may each of you be blessed with a Happy and Healthy
New Year.
Bruce Horovitz
Executive Director
— Bruce Horovitz

===== PAGE 31 =====
President’s Message
Have you ever noticed how many
members of our synagogue are involved
in the leadership of Jewish organizations
in our community? Doesn’t it make you
proud? As president of the Jacksonville
Jewish Center, it makes me extremely
proud on several levels. First, many of
these leaders are my friends, and I take
great pride in their accomplishments. Also,
I’m proud because they are helping the
Jewish community. Most of all, I’m proud
because the active participation of
members of the Center Family speaks volumes about our
success in developing and promoting involvement in all
aspects of Jewish life.
Our commitment to the future of Conservative
Jewish values begins with our youth. Come by the Center
anytime, any day and you are likely to see a flurry of
religious and cultural activities. Starting with our
Preschool, extending through the eighth grade of Solomon
Schechter Day School, and enhanced by our Religious
School, our children learn and live Judaism throughout
the school year, right on our campus. During the summer,
our Camp Neshama provides youngsters with a wonderful
recreational program that has a definite Jewish flavor.
Older children and teens can attend Camp Ramah, travel
around the country with USY-on-Wheels or go on a
pilgrimage to Israel, as part of the summer programs
sponsored by the Conservative Movement with the aid
of the Center Youth Commission. After their B ar or B at
Mitzvah, our students attend Beit Midrash and continue
their Jewish education through Confirmation.
It doesn’t stop there. We are always
looking for new and exciting programs for
our young families and for our not so young
families. Part of the enjoyment of being a
member at the Jacksonville Jewish Center
is the interaction of young and old. Much
of that integration is through education.
Whether it is one of the many programs
offered by the Adult Education Committee,
or a school program like Family University,
families of all ages are getting together.
The recently completed community demographic
study indicates that Jewish observance is fostered by
active membership in a synagogue. At the Jacksonville
Jewish Center, we help integrate home and synagogue
observance by providing twice-daily minyan, Shabbat and
Holiday Services, as well as wonderful Festival
celebrations like congregational Sukkot dinners, Passover
Seders and even an adult Purim gala.
Our members are our greatest assets. Like a big
Jewish family, we support and encourage each other and
plan for future growth.
As we enter a new year, 5764, it is time for
reflection. What have been our successes? What have
we accomplished? For the first time in its 42-year history,
the Solomon Schechter Day School graduated an eighth
grade class. In addition, it more than doubled the size of
the eighth grade class for this coming year. We adopted
the new Sim Shalom Siddur as our Shabbat and Daily
prayer book. We have completed the work in the DuBow-
Cohen Lobby, the Setzer Social Hall and the Fletcher-
Selber Auditorium as part of Restoration 2000, and we
refurbished the classrooms and hallways.
When I look forward to this next year, there are
many things I still want to achieve. Most of all I want to
engage the membership to become even more involved
in the life of our congregation. I want to challenge each
member to add Judaism to their lives and to do just one
additional thing this year to increase your involvement
and commitment to Judaism.
On behalf of my wife, Linda, and our children,
Lauren and Sasha, and from all of us at the Jacksonville
Jewish Center, L’Shana Tova.
— Philip Bloom
Philip Bloom
President

Center Choral Society
Reach-To-The-Beach
For over 55 years, the Center Choir has been enhancing
services on the High Holidays and Shavuot with moving liturgical
music. Over the years, they have given numerous concerts featuring
members of the choir, as well as nationally acclaimed soloists. Many
of the current members have been singing with this group for twenty
years or more. New members are always welcome. Call Raymond
Cohen 733-6979.
2003-2004 Choir

®The Reach-to-the-B each
project of the Jacksonville
Jewish Center is celebrating a
first birthday! Last fall, a few
synagogue members, who live
at the beach, met with Rabbi
Grundfast to plan some
educational and social initiatives for all Center
members who reside in the Jacksonville
Beaches area.
The first year’s events included two
programs on “Jewish Superstition and
Mysticism,” a Hanukkah Party with food,
songs and games, and a traditional Shabbat
Dinner with Shabbat songs and a wonderful
D’var Torah.
The final gathering of the year was a
Beach Party! The day was enriched by a lively
and enlightening talk by Judy Geller Nevel
about the history of Jews at the Beach.
Everyone attending said the talk was so
interesting and entertaining that we would have
to ask Judy for an encore next year! It was a
great way to close out our first year’s events.
Special thanks to this year’s planning
group, Carolyn Zisser, Rita Baumgarten,
Evelyn Peck, Judy DeArman, Linda
Ginsburg, and Ruth Rosenblatt. Each
member made unique and invaluable
contributions to this Center initiative.
Jewish Singles
The Jewish Singles program provides a place to “meet and
eat” for those living in Jacksonville and the surrounding area.
Dinners, and an occasional brunch, fill the calendar. Whether in
someone’s home or in a restaurant, these continue to be the most
popular gatherings.
A calendar of events is mailed several times a year, but the
information can also be found on the Jacksonville Jewish Federation
website at www.jaxjewish.org/singles.
For those who are far away from family, Jewish Singles helps
make friendships and matches. Another important service of this
program is providing home hospitality and “yom tov” meals for
those who would otherwise be alone for the holidays.
Funded by the Federation, this program continues to provide
important social and religious opportunities to Jewish singles in the
area.
More and varied programs are in the
works for the coming year. We enthusiastically
invite your participation in planning or just
attending an event. We welcome new and
returning members.
For information, questions, or suggestions
about the Reach-to-the-Beach events, please
contact Ruth Rosenblatt at 280-3115 or
rbrosenb@aol.com
For more information, contact Rhoda Goldstein at 292-1000.

Phyllis Goldberg
HAZAK! From strength! That was the message of this
year’s JTS Torah Fund Drive ... and that is exactly what your
Sisterhood did, with the enthusiasm, dedication and
commitment of every member who participated.
Sisterhood programs and projects promote education,
social action and religious observance. Through the annual
Torah Fund Campaign, we provide support for the Jewish
Theological Seminary and the Ziegler School of Rabbinic
Studies. At this year’s Torah Fund Luncheon, the “Horty T.
Gendzier Woman of Achievement” award was presented to
Phyllis Goldberg, past Sisterhood President, Center Board
member, Simhat Torah Woman of Valor, community leader,
and President-Elect of the Florida Branch of Women’s League of Conservative Judaism
- a strong woman indeed.
We are proud to offer financial support to Center schools and youth groups
through our continued donations to the Youth Fund, which offers scholarships for
Camp Ramah, USY on Wheels, and summer programs in Israel. This year Sisterhood
made a pledge to the Preschool Playground for a gazebo as part of a major renovation
plan. Our support also included providing snacks for High Holidays, apples and candy
for Simhat Torah, and hamentaschen for Purim.
Among the successful fund raising projects were the sale of Rosh Hashanah
flowers and cards, Nachas Tax and the Sisterhood Judaica Shop, which provides the
congregation and community with beautiful gift and ritual items, and whose proceeds
benefit Sisterhood programs. Perhaps our most successful fund-raising project was
the Annual Donor. This event raised over $6,000.00 for the Center Building Fund.
Educational and religious programs included enlightening monthly seminars led
by Rabbi Grundfast. Our members and their daughters demonstrated their many talents
and abilities during our spiritually uplifting Sisterhood Shabbat, which this year
coincided with Women’s League 40th Anniversary celebration. We also promoted
the Henry Kramer Library with several informative book reviews after Shabbat Services,
as well as a contribution that will provide much needed shelving for growing collections.
Sisterhood is thriving with over 360 members. Our monthly meetings were
interesting and well attended. Programs ranged from women’s health issues, shul
decorum, Feng Shui, to our own Susan DuBow’s giving us “a taste of Hollywood.”
Again this year, dedicated volunteers were recognized at each meeting. Robin Allerding,
Gayle Bailys, Pollie Copans, Beverly Geller, Rhoda Goldstein, Vivian Kaplan, Hilda
Lewit, Peggy Organes, Martha Savage, Hilda Warfield, Jean Weinberg and Elissa Vining
were among Sisterhood’s “Valued Volunteers.”
Jeanine Rogozinski
President
L to r: Pollie Copans, Martha Savage, Hilda Lewit, Vivian Kaplan,
Jean Weinberg and Hilda Warfield were among the valued
Sisterhood volunteers recognized at our monthly meetings.
A personal expression of gratitude goes to all the
officers, committee chairs and board members for being the
quintessential volunteers who always put Sisterhood first in
their lives.
In this coming year, let us embrace our responsibility to
our organization, our synagogue, our families, our future.
Through the act of volunteering, nothing is impossible, and our
success in enhancing the Jewish Community around us is
infinite. The Sisterhood Board and I hope to see a lot more of
you next year.
Chaim, Rachel, Erin, Jonathan, Danielle, and I wish you

and happiness.
— Jeanine Rogozinski

Men’s Club Man of the Year Banquet
On Sunday morning, October 27, Moti Demri was teased, taunted and lovingly
roasted by some of his closest friends. It was “No Problem” to honor him as the
Center Men’s Club’s 4th “Man of the Year,” for his longstanding service to the Men’s
Club, the Jacksonville Jewish Center and the Jewish community.
Evan Yegelwel, chairman of this event and last year’s honoree, planned a delightful
program which included a brunch buffet by Margo’s Catering. Moti was a good sport
and a great time was had by all.
The Man of the Year Banquet is the club’s biggest annual fundraiser. All proceeds
benefit the Men’s Club’s “Horty T. Gendzier Summer Scholarship Fund” that helps
needy Jewish children attend Camp Ramah and USY Pilgrimage programs.
In recognition of their achievement, Yad Shel
Chai recipients receive a certificate and
personalized “yad, ” Torah pointer.
Men’s Club Yad Shel Chai Award
In 1998, Center Men’s Club instituted this award-winning program
to encourage youngsters to continue reading Torah after their Bar or Bat
Mitzvah. Teens who read a minimum of 18 (chai) portions by age 18 are
presented with an inscribed Torah pointer (yad) and a certificate. Over
the years, many teens have enrolled in this program, and the following
have received the award: Jordan Allerding, Sarah Blankstein, Daniel
Heller, Jonathan Heller, Lauren Bloom, Crista Cohen, Jared Fleet, Aaron
Finck, Ben Finck, Seth Finck, Mark Frisch, Rachel Gerber, Max
Horovitz, Sam Horovitz, Debra Mizrahi, Dena Mizrahi, Jonathan
Mizrahi, Aliza Morris, Lindsay Morris, David Organes, Daniel Passen,
Lisa Rand, Avi Richman, Jessica Rogozinski and Rachel Rogozinski.
For more information regarding this program, contact Randall Smith at
221-8061.

Organizations
Center Men’s Club
The Jacksonville Jewish Center
Men’s Club is dedicated to the
enrichment of Center life and the
Jacksonville Jewish community. Men’s
Club members work together
supporting, sponsoring and participating
in programs that bring meaning to our
youth, companionship to our elders, and
involvement in our community.
Center Men’s Club is also an
active member of the Federation of
Jewish Men’s Clubs, an international
organization dedicated to the ideals,
philosophy and
traditions of
Conservative Judaism.
Among the successful
national programs that
we participate in is the
Yom Hashoah Yellow
Candle program. Each
year we distribute
hundreds of Holocaust
Memorial candles to
families of our
congregation. Another
program, “Hearing
Men’s Voices” is a
series of workshops for discussing issues
of significance to Jewish men in today’s
world. Topics for the coming year will
cover family, religion, society and
health, in thought provoking and
fulfilling agendas led by leading experts
and professionals.
We encourage our post Bar/Bat
Mitzvah teens to continue reading Torah
and reward those who read 18 or more
portions by age 18 with the Yad Shel Chai
(Hand of Life) award.
Sunday morning programs featured varied
and informative speakers.
Center Men’s Club’s “Horty T.
Gendzier Summer Scholarship Fund”
provides the financial resources for
children to attend Camp Ramah or other
Jewish enrichment programs, and
honors the memory of Horty Gendzier,
who was so instrumental in the
pioneering of these programs. Funding
is provided in large part by proceeds
from the annual “Man of the Year”
banquet.
We support the Jacksonville
Jewish Federation, Jacksonville Family
and Community
Services and the
community at large
through tzedakah
programs and
volunteer efforts.
We are
visible friends of
our Center, with
programs like
selling and building
sukkot for our
Center families,
and helping to
decorate the Center’s Goldman Sukkah.
You can find Men’s Club members
grilling lunch at the Lag B’omer Picnic
every year. Our members are the friendly
ushers who greet you at services on
Shabbat and Holidays. Men’s Club
members sponsor, lead and participate
in Men’s Club Shabbat and Armed
Forces Shabbat.
The Men’s Club is also a great way
for friends to have fun. Every summer
we unite for the infamous deep sea
fishing trip, and take our families to
sporting events, such as a Jacksonville
Suns baseball game. In the fall we “kick
off’ our new year with a membership
drive featuring games of chance and
raffles, while we watch a Jacksonville
Jaguars away game on a big screen TV.
All this and more is waiting you if
you are at least 18 years old, male, and
a member of the Jacksonville Jewish
community. Join now. We welcome your
fellowship and participation.
— Mike Herring, President

and (r) Mike Herring

Shabbat/Holiday Ushers
Fred Blum & Tom Spriggs, Chairs
During the High Holidays and on Shabbat and holidays,
friendly volunteer members serve as ambassadors to Center
congregants by helping with seating, guiding and acknowledging
newcomers, and welcoming regular worshippers. Ushers help to
maintain synagogue decorum, which preserves the beauty of
the service for all of us. We thank all of our ushers for their
efforts throughout the year.

Daily Minyan Captains
Traditionally, public worship requires a minyan, a
quorum of ten men. Only in the presence of a minyan may the
Torah be read or the Kaddish prayer be recited.
Our dedicated minyan captains ensure that there is a
minyan twice every single day of the year. It is often a hard
and thankless job. It requires hours of phoning to coordinate
attendance.
We thank those who served as minyan captains during
the 2002-2003 season: Jack Bettman, Robert Handmaker,
Jack Mizrahi, Fred Kupperman, David Schmerer, Russell
Selevan, Jack Silverman, Edward Tannen, Evan Yegelwel,
David Zavon, Sandy Zimmerman and Seeman Zimmerman.
It is because of them that you can recite kaddish
when you mourn or observe yarhzeit. We owe the captains
not only our thanks, but also our participation, in order to
continue providing a minyan for each service.
To emphasize the mitzvah aspect of his Bar Mitzvah,
Ben Morse become a regular member of the Monday
morning minyan. He also sent post cards to men in our
congregation inviting them to join. Among those who
responded were classmates Eddie Norton, Kyle Soloway
and Kyle Vining.
Please become a “regular” for at least one minyan a
week. Call Marco Rand, Religious Committee Chair, at
737-9761.
Henry Kramer Library & Resource Center
Minnie Schreiber, Chair
Committee: Rabbi Joseph Hirsch, Svetlana Goldiner,
Blanche Slott and Roselyn Selber
Assistants: Debbie Shacter and Stephanie Shacter
A library will be only a resting place for books, if the
books are not accessible to readers. Accessibility requires
proper classification, carding shelving and monitoring.
Such was the monumental task that May Goldie
Stillman, of blessed memory, performed for the Tofield
Memorial Library. Every Sunday morning was dedicated to
working in the library, as it grew and became the Henry
Kramer Library and Resource Center.
May Goldie’s illness and recent death ended her library
service of many years as co-chairman, but the library itself
will be a constant reminder of her dedication and devotion.
The Jacksonville Jewish Center will always be grateful.
From its humble beginnings in 1959, the Henry Kramer
Library and Resource Center, which includes the Solomon
Schechter Day School Library and the Tofield Reading Room,
has developed into the splendid library that it is through the
work of May Goldie Stillman and countless other synagogue
members.

Committees
Shabbat and Holiday Liturgy
Yitzhak Ben-Moshe, Baal Tefillah
Hearing Raymond Cohen’s beautiful tenor
voice during the Yamim Nora ’im is one of my most
enduring memories of growing up at the Jacksonville
Jewish Center. There seemed to be an extra measure
of holiness to the prayers when Raymond and the
Center Choral Society would accompany Cantor
Marton, z’l, on Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur. I’m
pleased to count Raymond as a colleague and a friend
now, and I’m delighted that this year’s edition of the yearbook is dedicated to him
and his years of service to the Center.
The Mahzor reads “...repentance, prayer and tzedakah avert the unfavorable
decree.” Indeed, one of the main purposes of Jewish prayer is to inspire repentance
and tzedakah, or righteousness. By praying and confessing as a
community, in the first person plural, we reaffirm the rabbinical dictum “All of
Israel are responsible for one another.”
Every year when the Temple was in existence, the Kohen Gadol would pray
on Yom Kippur for the well being of all the People of Israel. My prayer for the
coming year is that it be one of health and prosperity for us all, and a year of peace
in the Land of Israel and throughout the world. From D’vorah, lian and myself,
Ishanah tovah tikkateivu ut’hateimu.
— Yitzhak Ben-Moshe
Religious Committee
Marco Rand, Chairman
The Religious Committee is in the honored position of guiding many of the
ritual functions that are the pulse of our congregation. Whether it is helping to
ensure the reliability of the twice-daily minyan, overseeing the standards of our
services, or coordinating High Holiday honors, the Religious Committee’s work
is often unheralded, but nonetheless vital to the daily life and times of the
Jacksonville Jewish Center. Acting in concert with the Rabbi, it is the job of this
committee to see to it that the rituals of the synagogue continue to conform to the
strong traditions of our congregation and to the highest standards of the
Conservative movement.
Our congregation is grateful to Dave Schmerer for his strong leadership as
chair of this committee during a period of significant transition at the Center.
Special kudos are due to Bob Bossen for his continuing stalwart work as our Gabbai
coordinator - this past year saw the inclusion of women in the Gabbai corps. This
year’s High Holiday honors subcommittee was led by Edward Tannen.
We look forward to learning with and working with the congregation as we
face the many potential challenges and changes that loom on the horizon.
Religious Committee members in 2002-2003 were: Neil Abramson,
Yitzhak Ben-Moshe, Jack Bettman, Abe Bielski, Daniel Blankstein, Fred
Blum, Robert Bossen, Wendy Brezin, Moti Demri, Etta Fialkow, Janis Fleet,

Sandler, David Schmerer, Leonard Selber, Joseph Shacter, Mark Shorstein,
Edward Tannen, Dan Wohl.
— Marco Rand
Shabbat Torah Readers
Scott Zimmerman,
Ritual Director
The Greatest Commandment
The Talmud teaches that the
mitzvah of Talmud Torah (Jewish
learning) is the greatest of all mitzvot.
Because study leads to action, and
because understanding and information
are prerequisites for performing
mitzvot, Talmud Torah contains the
potential for all the other mitzvot. What
we leam is who we become.
For centuries, we have been
known as the people of the Book
because of our special relationship
with the Book of books, the Torah.
While other ancient peoples worshiped
by sacrificing people or animals, we
developed a form of worship that
centered on reading as a sacred act.
The survival of Judaism depends
on something as frail and resilient as
learning and teaching. Whether in a
classroom, a synagogue, or a home, we
add our voices to the process that is
Torah by studying our sacred writings
and traditions, by joining in discussion
and debate with our fellow Jews.
I would like to thank the many
members of our congregation whose
dedication has allowed us to maintain
the high level of participation in Torah
reading that our synagogue has
achieved. With the commitment and
encouragement of our synagogue
organizations and their leaders, we will
preserve our standards for future
generations. I would like to thank Ted
Gross for his many years of guidance
and encouragement as well as all of our
teachers for their continued support and
cooperation and wish you all a heartfelt
Shanah Tovah.
— Scott Zimmerman

===== PAGE 49 =====
Committees
Adult Education
Etta Fialkow, chair
This year’s adult activities offered a variety of
educational opportunities - some familiar, some new.
Hebrew Literacy is a staple of the curriculm. Etta
Fialkow taught classes for beginners. Students who could
not read any of the letters in the Hebrew alefbet, found
that in just a few short lessons they could read some
prayers. Arlene Yegelwel worked with other students
helping them to better improve their reading skills. Lorrain
Federman introduced a new program of teaching reading
skills and, at the same time, the meaning of many of the
words used in the prayers. Marc Leventhal continued a
class in conversational Hebrew that he began last year.
Rabbi Stephen Grundfast taught a number of
courses this year. Enlightening, bi-monthly Talmud class
used the book Swimming in the Sea ofTalmudby Michael
Katz and Gershon Schwartz. At monthly “Lunch and
Learn” sessions, students ate and studied various texts
with Rabbi Grundfast at the office of Shorstein and
Shorstein. Under the auspices of Center Sisterhood, Rabbi
Grundfast continued his seminars for and about Jewish
women, with discussions of Ketuvim, the Writings found
in the Tanakh. Continuing his post-Confirmation program,
Rabbi Grundfast hosted several informal dinners with
12th graders to discuss topics of interest to young adults.
Rabbi Grundfast also taught an introduction to
Judaism and Jewish life for those seeking either conversion
to Judaism or more knowledge about their Jewish heritage.
In January and February, Rabbi Grundfast conducted
a special four-week mini series that concentrated on the
hows and whys of our Jewish prayer service. He
discussed the Siddur, the structure of the prayer service,
the development of the synagogue, the morning blessings,
the Shema, the Amidah and all the variations of the
Kaddish. As a hands-on part of the class, he gave lessons
on the proper way to make a Torah aliyah, how to lift
and tie the Torah, and spoke on when and how to bow.
Rabbi Joseph Hirsch taught a six-week course in
February and March that explored the political and cultural
spheres of the history of the Jewish people. He broke
the classes into six periods of Jewish history: the Biblical,
Second Temple, Talmudic, Geonic, Medieval and Modem
Periods. Rabbi Hirsch recently joined the Jacksonville
Community, coming from Palm Coast.
The Adult Education
Committee instituted the
Setzer-Levit Family Program
Series, an endowment to the
Jacksonville Jewish Center by
Leah and Milton Levit as a
memorial to their mothers,
Hannah Setzer and Dora Levit.
It is a complement to the Setzer-
Levit Lecture Series that has
provided world renown
speakers of topical Jewish issues in memory of their
fathers, Benjamin Setzer and Joseph Levit. On December
8, the entire Jewish community was invited to an evening
with guest performer Rahel Musleah. The program,
“Jews in Calcutta? Is that near Kalamazoo?” began
with a buffet dinner featuring Kosher Indian Cuisine.
The seventh generation of a Calcutta family, Musleah
opened the window to the rich, but little-known, heritage
of the Jews of India. She creatively engaged our
children’s participation through slides, song and stories.
The Setzer-Levit Lecture
Series brought award-winning
journalist, Stephen Dubner, to
our congregation and the students
of Beit Midrash. Dubner spoke
on his life experience, and of
returning to his Jewish roots.
Barbara Pakula ably chaired this
important event.
Etta Fialkow
29

Professor Cherry delivered
three diverse lectures: “How
Jews have Responded to
Darwinian Evolution, “Kashrut
in the Twenty-first Century -
should vegetarianism be a
mitzvah?” and a talk on Jewish
mysticism. Shabbaton
Weekend is underwritten by the
Marilyn and Louis Safer

memory of Marilyn and Lou Safer by their children Eliot
Safer, Cynthia Baron, Deena Richman, and Shana Temel.

Special Events
Simhat Torah Honorees
The High Holiday season reaches its joyous climax on Simhat Torah, the last day of the festival
of Sukkot. Because of our perennial love of the Torah, it has been referred to as Israel’s “bride”. On
Simhat Torah, we bring to a close the annual cycle of the reading of the Torah and immediately begin
anew. An ancient tradition evolved of honoring worthy men by calling them to the Torah for the last
reading, Hatan Torah, and the beginning portion, Hatan Bereshit. In our synagogue tradition, we
also honor the contributions made by a “Woman of Valor”.
David Schmerer
Hatan Torah
David
Schmerer is one
of the nicest guys
you’ll ever meet.
Being affable is
also a quality that
Dave draws upon
to enlist the aid
of others. He’s
both a devoted volunteer and a very
effective leader.
David Schmerer was born in
Miami Beach in 1952. He received a
BA in government from FSU and a BT,
cum laude, in industrial technology
from UNF. He is a Safety & Health
Consultant with Zenith Insurance.
When the Schmerers moved to
our community in 1981, Dave found
that the Center offered just the right
mix of traditional Jewish observance
and a wide variety of activities. He
immediately became active in Family
Council, and youth would become a
focal point for his volunteer efforts in
the years that followed.
At the heart of it all is Dave’s
deep love of Judaism. He expresses it
in his own observance, and in the
attention he gives religious life at the
Center. David has taught in our
Religious School, Hebrew High and in
Junior Congregation. He is a minyan
captain, Shabbat usher, gabbai, bass
soloist in the Center Choir and past
chairman of the Religious committee
For five years, Dave was
president of the Center Men’s Club. He
was the driving force behind the
creation of the Horty T. Gendzier
Summer Scholarship Fund, as well as
many other successful fundraising,
social and communal projects that
benefit our congregation.
Fred Pozin
Hatan Bereshit
Fred Pozin
has a real head for
business and a
genuine heart for
the welfare of our
congregation.
This winning
combination has
made him
invaluable as the
Center’s Financial Vice President.
Beginning in 2000, and continuing with
this administration, Fred’s tireless
efforts have maintained the fiscal
strength of our synagogue.
Fred Pozin has the hotel business
in his blood. He was bom in Miami
Beach, and at a young age, relocated
to Gainesville, where his family built
and operated the University Motel.
Later in Orange Park, they built and
operated the Holiday Inn. After
attending the Hotel Restaurant School
at Florida State University, Fred began
his career with the Hyatt Hotel
Corporation and served in numerous
management positions.
In the early 80s, Fred returned to
Jacksonville to open and operate the
Ramada Inn Mandarin and Comedy Zone.
He met and married Wendy Margol and
became active at the Center.
With Fred’s business acumen and
dedication to Jewish education, he was
a natural choice to co-chair the 1997
Center Raffle for Education, and other
fundraising events. Most notably, Fred
lent his Comedy Club for an exclusive
performance to benefit Hadassah.
Active on our Board of Directors, Fred
served on the house and finance
committees before accepting the
position of Financial Vice President,
which he still holds.
Phyllis Goldberg
Woman of Valor
Phyllis
Goldberg is an
empowered
woman, dedicated
to Jewish life and
education. She is
poised, assured
and self-confident.
She is a loyal
friend and delightful companion. A
strong sense of propriety guides her
every action. She is the essence of the
Woman of Valor “robed in strength and
dignity; abounding in wisdom; modest,
her work proclaims her praises.”
Born in Chicago, Phyllis was
raised in Jacksonville from age 4. She
received a bachelor’s degree from the
University of Pennsylvania, and a
master’s degree at Columbia. She
married Larry Goldberg and began a
family in New York, but was soon drawn
back to Jacksonville.
Phyllis retired from the computer
profession to become a “professional
volunteer.” The Center has been the
beneficiary of her time and talent for
organization for over 20 years. She is a
past VP of Membership, long-standing
Board member, and has served on the
Adult Education, Performing Artists
and Rabbi Search committees, among
others.
Over the years, Phyllis has been
a leader and driving force for women’s
issues. In Center Sisterhood, she served
as Education VP, Torah Fund chair and
President. She distinguished herself in
numerous positions for the Florida
Branch of Women’s League for
Conservative Judaism and sits on the
International Board. Phyllis has served
Hadassah as chapter co-chair, and
earned its Chai Award.

Special Events
2003 Center Raffle for Education
“OOTFoyDfeiDofyoufc”
This year’s raffle raised the second highest total in Center history.
Once again, the big winners were the children of the Samuel & Esther
Galinsky Educational Programs who will benefit from the funds raised
by this major endeavor.
Amy Goodman and Faye Mizrahi, Raffle Co-Chairs, are to be
highly commended for their dedication and tireless efforts to make this
event a sensational success. Not only were the proceeds large, so was
the attendance at the Raffle Brunch. Over 400 people enjoyed a fabulous
brunch, beautifully prepared and presented by Margo’s Catering.
The brunch featured a wonderful program that included jazz music,
by the Scott Foster Trio. An enjoyable fashion show was staged by
Emilie Christenson and her Ponte Vedra store, Kyds. The adorable
models, from among the students of Center schools, were professionally
groomed by Daryl Powers Salon & Spa. Photographer, Meg Pryor,
took runway shots of every model. Thanks to Susan DuBow for all her
help coordinating the fashion show.
Honorary Raffle Chairs, Helen & Michael DuBow, ticket sellers
and event committees share the appreciation of our congregation for
this wonderful fundraising event. Thank you to Richard Ford and the
maintenance staff, as well as Inez Achord, Rhoda Goldstein, Lori
Schoettler and other Center staff for all their help.
Of course, the real gratitude goes to the patrons, sponsors and
ticket purchasers whose generous support made all of this possible.
Rabbi Dov Kentof Honored for Educational Excellence
The Jacksonville Jewish Center is pleased to
announce that Rabbi Dov Kentof, Director
Eméritas of Education & Youth, is this year’s
recipient of the Rabbi David Gaffney Leadership
in Education Award. For over 20 years, Rabbi
Kentof instilled a sense of Jewish identity in the
children of our congregation, the Jacksonville
community and throughout the Southeast, through
innovative programs, a unique educational style and
genuine concern for the individual. Mazel tov to
Dov & Alina Kentof and family on this well
deserved honor.

a desirable choice.

4th Annual JJC Golf Classic
A Big Win for Scholarships.
The Annual JJC Golf Classic, played at the Ponte Vedra Ocean Course,
is one of only three elite charitable events held at the prestigious course. Not
only was it a great financial success, but a GREAT TIME was had by all who
teed off in glorious weather, on a beautiful course. Camaraderie was high and
the competition was keen. Congratulations to all.
The credit for this outstanding program goes to Scott
Allerding, tournament chairman, Lori Schoettler, Center
administrative liaison and the committee. Additional thanks
goes to a great crew of tournament-day volunteers: Robin
Allerding, Helen DuBow, Michelle Margol and Jeanine
Rogozinski.
The Horty T. Gendzier Cup was presented to the
tournament winners: Bill Dennis, Bob Sarvis, Steve
Silverman and Rich Zanghetti.
Horty Gendzier was a major force in Jewish education at the Center.
Her lifelong commitment to Jewish education in Jacksonville paved the way
for countless numbers of children to experience the beauty, worth and
importance of leading a Jewish life. Fulfilling Horty Gendzier s vision, the
mission of the JJC Golf Classic is to make education at the Solomon Schechter
Day School accessible to all Jewish children. This major fundraising event
provides scholarships to any child in need of financial assistance, regardless
of synagogue affiliation.
Horty T. Gendzier CT
Above: Edith Horovitz (l) and her father, Sheldon Gendzier
(r), pose with the receipients (ctr) of the Horty I Gendzier
Cup, presented to the winning team.

Holiday Celebrations
Hanukkah Happenings
Annual Lag B’Omer Picnic
Nearly 300 people crowded the synagogue for the annual congregational
party which included activity booths run by the Religious School, dinner by
Margo’s Catering and over two dozen fabulous craft exhibits.
Over two dozen “Reach-to-the-Beach” members had a grand time making
latkes and playing dreidel at a dinner for those who live at the beach.
Families poured into the Center
Recreational Park & Campgrounds for
the official opening of Camp Neshama,
at the Lag B’Omer picnic in May. It was a
wonderful afternoon filled with fun, food
friends and “Mitzvah Clowns.”
Purim-a-Plenty
Queen Esther, Haman and a variety of other
characters had a blast at the Preschool and Day
School programs.
No one partied better than the adults. “My
Big, Fat Shushan Wedding” was the zaniest Purim
dinner and program on record!

Lifecycle Events
Burial and Mourning
Center Cemetery
The Center owns and maintains two cemeteries adjacent to the Evergreen
Cemetery in North Jacksonville. Both are open daylight hours every day except
Shabbat and Jewish holidays. To reach the Old Cemetery, travel north on North
Main Street to Winona. Make a right on Winona and go until you reach Gate 5.
The Old Cemetery is on the left. To reach the New Cemetery, travel north on
North Main Street to 43rd Street. Make a
right on 43rd Street and the entrance is at
the next right, which is Liberty Street.
This year, middle school students of
the Solomon Schechter Day School learned,
through the Mitzvah Program, about the
respectful care of the dead, including tending
of burial sites. On a visit to the Old Cemetery,
they discovered that several family plots no
longer had loved ones to maintain them. The
students rolled up their sleeves and, with great care and respect, cleaned the
neglected headstones of a family that been laid to rest more than 50 years ago.
We are proud and grateful to these children for performing an important mitzvah.
Future plans for the cemetery include improvements to the entrances, as
well as additional landscaping. Contributions can be made to the Cemetery Fund
in honor or in memory of loved ones. All donations will be used to enhance and
maintain our cemeteries.
We thank the volunteers
who serve on this
important committee:
Elyse Whitman, chairperson
Barbara Cantor
Charlotte Fialkow
Stacey Goldring
Dr. Jeffrey Goldstein
Stuart Hecht
Fred Kupperman
Leonardo Maiman
Morrie Osterer
Marsha Pollock
Nathan Sandler
Blanche Slott
Evan Yegelwel
Seeman Zimmerman
Students from Solomon Schechter Day
Schools Mitzvah Program cleaned
unattended headstones.
Hevra Kaddisha
Officers 2003-2004
President
Nathan C. Sandler
Vice President/Treasurer
Bob Bossen
Vice President
Fred Kupperman
Taharah Committee Chairs
Ilse Gottlieb
Sally Becker
Ava Axelrod
Vice President/Secretary
Naomie Bossen
Judaism is a faith that embraces all of life. Death is part of the cycle of life.
Just as Judaism leads us through moments of joy, so too does it lead us through
moments of grief at a death within our family.
At the time of a death, painful questions and concerns are natural. In the
midst of great loss we must deal with the procedures for proper burial. It is
perplexing to know how to care for the deceased.
It is then that the Hevra Kaddisha fulfills its purpose. First, the tahara,
preparing the deceased for burial, is performed by a committee made up of
caring lay members of the Jewish community. The customs for physical cleansing
and preparation are guided by the precept of respect for the dead mandated by
the Torah. Our members also recite the required prayers asking God for forgiveness
for any sins that may have been committed by the deceased, as well as praying
that the All Merciful guard them in eternal life.
The Jewish community of Jacksonville can feel assured, knowing that we
have a committee that is ready and w illing at all times to be of help. Call any
officer or member for immediate information on our services. WE ARE HERE
FOR YOU.
—Nathan C. Sandler, president

===== PAGE 103 =====
The Samuel & Esther Galinsky Educational Programs —
Early Childhood Department
located in the Selevan Preschool and Day Care Center
Message from the Director
Dale Schemer
Director
A recent study of Jewish identity development found that “Jewishness in adulthood
appears related to a strong orientation towards Jewish life in childhood. When conveyed in
the early years, the message about the importance of being Jewish persists into adulthood.”
The staff of the Jacksonville Jewish Center Preschool feels a strong professional and
personal responsibility to provide that message by offering a Jewish education in which our
children are not just Jewish on the holidays, but feel their Jewishness in everything they do.
Our goal is to give our young children the best possible start in life. We strive to
provide them with not only the important cognitive and social skills, but also a solid Jewish
educational foundation.
Robin Morris
and Michelle Margol
Judaica Teachers
Janet Husney
Extended Day Coordinator
We know that this year, as we have for the past 61 years, we will provide our Jewish
children with warm and supportive teachers who offer stimulating and developmentally
appropriate activities and materials. But most importantly, we will provide
them with an sense of affiliation and belonging that will last a lifetime.
Shirley Thacker
Secretary

— The Samuel & Esther Galinsky Educational Programs —
Solomon Schechter Day School
located in the Gordon-Hecht-Bossen Education Center
Message from the Principal
The Solomon Schechter Day School has existed for forty-two
years. For many families, the longevity of the school and its record of
placing students in the very best public and private secular school
programs are critical ingredients in choosing S S D S. The efficiency
of a dual-language program is not questioned since our graduates
demonstrate remarkable academic prowess in addition to strong social
and emotional Jewish identity skills.
What makes our institution different from others? Our graduates!
They leave SSDS with a set of experiences, skills, values and a
profound sense of who they are within the context of American society
that cannot be replicated by other area institutions. Their uniqueness
is grounded in our educational program that combines the normative
experiences of what excellent schooling is compiled with the distinctive
aspect of developing a spiritual component that is unique to being
Jewish. We seek to nurture the totality of the human experience for Jewish children in an environment
filled with caring, support, wonder, and excitement. As one parent said to me, “My children go to school
happy and enthusiastic every day. What more can one ask?”
What makes us so special? What are the hallmarks of our strength?
• Care is taken by all to meet academic needs.
• Students feel cared for and respected.
• The environment is warm and intimate.
• In a year fraught with fear and disturbing news in the world,
the school gave its students a sense of security and well-being.
• It has the right balance between General and Jewish studies.
• There is a strong academic and comprehensive curriculum.
• The celebration of Jewish holidays is a very positive and
dynamic experience.
• The school enhances a child’s love and understanding of
all things Jewish.
• Students get a strong, positive Jewish identity.
• Jewish calendar days are a part of the routine, and not incidental.
It is clear that our dual-studies program is considered a unique asset for
the development of our students. It promotes academic excellence and the joy
of being Jewish.
Andy White
School Secretary
Willard M. Kennedy
Principal

The Parent - Teacher Association of the Solomon Schechter Day School and the Center
Preschool is committed to providing the very best for our students. PTA enhances the
educational experience with quality programs and services.
The following are some of the great programs, services and fundraisers that PTA
provides throughout the year for the students: Holiday Observances, Red Ribbon Week (drug
awareness), Library and Art Assistants, Vision Screening, Purim Carnival, Magazine Sale,
Gift Wrapping Sale and much more.
As you can see, PTA has many great plans for this school year. An integral part_of our
success lies in the hands of our volunteers. PTA is successful because of the wonderful
parents and teachers who join and support it. PTA volunteers are appreciated for their time
and efforts.
This year, I have the honor of being PTA president. It has personal significance, as my
mother, Alix Levy, was PTA president of Solomon Schechter Day School in 1968. I have
many fond memories of my mothers’ involvement in PTA . I remember the excitement of
seeing her in the hallways at school or working PTA programs. What a wonderful legacy we
can leave our children; fond memories of our involvement in their lives.
I look forward to another exciting and busy year.
Warmest regards,
— Allison Bailys

The Samuel & Esther Galinsky Educational Programs
Center Religious School
A Message from the Director
The goal of the Jacksonville Jewish
Center Religious School is to educate and
encourage our children as they grow and
take their places among other young
Jewish adults in our community.
The staff is dedicated and nurturing
Students learn through the use of music,
art, drama, mitzvah projects and fun hands-
on holiday projects, as well as excellent
classroom instruction. There are family
programs throughout the year.
Our children also participate in
synagogue-wide programs and many are
eager to lead portions of Shabbat services
in the adult as well as youth services.
In keeping with the new United Synagogue “Framework
of Excellence,” we have reorganized our Religious School
program to include a Sunday component.
Starting this fall, instruction for all grades will include
classes on Sundays from 10 a.m. to 12 noon. The Sunday
program will encompass an exciting variety of arts and crafts,
music and biblical literature, as well as participation in many
creative, hands-on Jewish holiday and life-cycle
dramatizations. In addition, students in the Alef (grade 3)
through Dalet (grade 6) classes will participate each week in
a “Student Minyan” led by Rabbi Grundfast. The Religious
School will round out the curriculum by interfacing with
existing Center Youth and Recreational programs to open
new avenues for interaction.
Optional Family and Parent
Education opportunities will be
incorporated several times throughout the
year. Parents are also encouraged to take
advantage of weekly adult education
classes, monthly brunches and special
events to be held at the Center on Sundays
during Religious School hours.
Weekday classes will continue for
students in grades 3 - 7 on Mondays and
Wednesdays from 4:45-6:45 p.m. The
focus will be on Hebrew instruction, which
will include conversational classes for
those who are further advanced in their
Hebrew studies. These classes are
designed to keep these students challenged
and motivated to proceed at their own rate.
Also resuming will be our successful specialty
programs. The new 2nd grade Mechinah class, which meets
on Sunday and Wednesday, is a bridge into the full Religious
School program. The popular 7th grade Etgar class provides
educational opportunities that capture the interest of young
teens. Weekly Junior and Pre-Junior Congregations will be
held every Shabbat. In addition, a monthly Religious School
Family Shabbat program will take place.
I look forward to extending this wonderful opportunity
to your child and your family! For more information, or to
register your child in any class, please call 268-4200, ext.
145, or stop by the Center Religious School office.
— Lois Tompkins, Religious School Director
Melissa Gibbons
Youth & Education Secretary

Consecration
Shabbat morning, February 22,2003
For weeks, students of the Aleph class of the Religious
School and the 1st grade of the Solomon Schechter Day
School prepared a very special program for this milestone
in their Jewish education. Each student received a certificate
and a sweet treat from PTA traditionally given to mark a sweet
beginning to their formal Hebrew education. Beautifully
covered siddurim, prayerbooks, were presented to the
students by their parents. In addition, Center Sisterhood gave
each student a bound collection of Leagrams containing well
wishes from family and friends. Todah Rabah to all the
teachers: Rivka Cohen, Paula Horn, Carole Goldberg,
Bonnie Loeser, liana Manasse, Robin Morris and Eta
Perras.

Mechinah- 2nd Grade Graduation
May 1,2003
Students of the 2nd grade Mechinah class were
promoted into the full Religious School during a ceremony
that included receiving their very own mini-torahs and
certificates. Students (pictured 1 to r) Justin Vitiello, Josh
Stevens, Jonathan Waring, Charlie DuBow and (not
pictured) Blair DeCrispino performed newly-learned
blessings and prayers, and read paragraphs they had written
about each Jewish holiday and derech eretz. The Mechinah
class was successfully initiated this past year as a program
to “jump-start” Hebrew skills and to introduce students to
the afternoon school with a Sunday/Wednesday schedule.
Many thanks to teachers Karen Morse and Daphne
Woodard for their hard work.

Confirmation Class of 2003
6 & 7 Sivan • June 5-7, 2003
The Biblical festival of Shavuot commemorates the giving of the Torah and Ten Commandments to the
Jewish people. It is fitting that the festival should be celebrated with the accompanying sense of commitment to
Jewish life that Confirmation represents. Our Confirmands demonstrated the knowledge they have gained through
completion of the Beit Midrash - Community Hebrew High by fully participating in Shavuot services. In addition,
students read essays they had prepared on the theme “What Judaism Means to Me.”
2003 Confirmands pictured with their teacher, Rabbi Stephen Grundfast: Jordan Axelrod, Geri Bernard,
Jon Bernhardt, Sarah Blankstein, Sasha Bloom, Robyn Blum, Leia Fixel, Marissa Hochrad, Max Horovitz,

Beit Midrash
Jacksonville Community
Hebrew High School
Pamela Fine Maman - Director
The Beit Midrash, Hebrew High School, program involves 8th - 12th
grade students throughout the community . Classes taught cover curriculum
from the following areas: Literature, Hebrew, Israel, Jewish Community,
Jewish Education, Jewish Ethics and Values, Jewish History, Judaic
Studies and Texts. Classes meet Wednesday evenings from 7-9 p.m. For
more information visit our website at www.beitmidrashjax org, or
call 448-5000.
