===== PAGE 121 =====
Center Youth Department
A Message from the Director
Gayle Bailys
Director
It is the goal of the Jacksonville Jewish Center Youth Department to offer a unique
opportunity to stimulate the spiritual and social growth and development of the children of
our congregation. This past year, with the help of the Youth Commission, the youth group
advisors and the youth group boards, a variety of religious, social, athletic and cultural
activities were offered. Opportunities were provided for our children to share fun and
distinctively Jewish experiences with their friends.
We are instilling in our children a sense of pride in their heritage, as well as a
commitment to the ideals of Jewish life. We are helping our young people to develop an
appreciation for our synagogue, and a willingness to work for its betterment. They are
learning to fulfill the social needs of our community, and to participate in many civic
activities. Together, we have experienced the gifts of mitzvot. It is our belief that the
future of Conservative Judaism can be secured through participation in innovative programs
designed to develop upcoming young Jewish leaders.
I’d like to thank all those who gave their time, support and help this past year. I look forward to sharing the
coming year with the youth of the Jacksonville Jewish Center.
— Gayle Bailys
Center Youth Commission
The Youth Commission oversees all youth organizations and programs
sponsored by the Jacksonville Jewish Center including Chalutzim, Kadima,
USY, Scouts and the Center Day Camp. The committee is made up of youth
group advisors, presidents of our clubs and caring Center members who
believe that the future of Conservative Judaism can be secured through
participation in innovative programs designed to develop upcoming Jewish
leaders.
In addition to membership in Center Youth Groups, the Youth
Commission encourages our youngsters to attend United Synagogue summer
programs, such as Camp Ramah, USY - on - Wheels, Ramah Seminar in
Israel and USY Poland/Israel Pilgrimage. These provide excellent
opportunities for our children to share wholesome, fun and uniquely Jewish
experiences with their peers from all over the United States. The Youth
Commission assists applicants with a variety of scholarships.
Through our College Outreach program, our college undergraduates
stay connected to the synagogue and community. Four times a year, at Rosh
Hashanah, Chanukah, Purim and Passover, care packages are sent that bring
warm wishes and promote holiday observance. Help us to stay in touch with
your children by keeping us updated on their school mailing and email
addresses. Thank you to Stella Finck for her long-standing devotion to this
project.
OUR MISSION
The purpose of the Youth Programs
of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is to
bridge the invisible gap between the home,
the school and the synagogue. All of our
youth activities combined offer a unique
opportunity to stimulate educational,
spiritual and social growth and
development within a Judaic environment.
To oversee these activities, the Youth
Commission and Youth Director, sets the
standards and policies for these programs.
The Youth Commission inducted new youth group
officers, board members and advisors at the annual
Youth Banquet held on Sunday, May 5. The brunch
program was dedicated to “Our Youth - Carrying the
Light into the Future. ”
— Kathy Osterer, Youth Commission Chair

===== PAGE 131 =====
Scouting
Cadette/Senior Girl Scout Troop 969
The World of Cadette/Senior Girl Scouting is an
exciting, challenging experience, that offers new
opportunities for girls to learn about themselves and the
world around them. Girls explore personal interests, develop
a healthy way of life, work on leadership skills and provide
service to their community.
Service is very important to Scouting, so this year
several girls participated in at least two events. Foster parents
have a very difficult job, so the Salvation Army held a holiday
party for their families. Our girls played with the youngest
children at the party, to give the parents a well-deserved
respite. This activity helped the girls earn the “Child Care”
interest patch. Later in the year, all the girls delivered dinner,
prepared by them, to the residents at the Ronald McDonald
House. The staff realized long ago that parents were too
exhausted at the end of a day at the hospital to cook dinner,
so organizations provide
dinner for the residents.
Preparing dinner helped
the girls earn the ‘Creative
Cookery’ interest patch.
Several new skills
were learned this year. A
former caterer taught
how to make edible
decorations, as part of the
“Creative Cookery”
interest patch. The girls
leaned about daycare
options by interviewing
several Moms, and
learned about making
Braille books from a
teacher at the Florida School for the Deaf and the Blind, for
the interest patch, “Child Care.” The girls have a head start
for future employment as they created resumes, for the
interest patch, “Leadership.” These interest patches offered
the girls opportunities to have fun, while learning about
themselves.
jobs and families, always a difficult task. They found out
about salary ranges and training required for five different
careers, as well as about two fields in which women are not
the majority.
Several girls also earned the “Cadette Girl Scout
Challenge” and our Senior girl earned the Senior Girl Scout
Challenge. Girl Scouts are challenged to be the best possible
person they can be. This involves knowing themselves,
relating to others, developing values, contributing to their
community, and knowing about Girl Scouting. The girls
participated in activities from each area, which form the basis
of the Challenge.
Three girls participated in a ski trip to Snowshoe
Mountain in Virginia, which was sponsored by our area
Gateway Council. For Florida girls, this was a real adventure.
They learned the basics of
skiing and had fun in an
environment unfamiliar to
them. Other national and
international trips, through
the Girl Scout’s “Wider
Opportunities” program,
help broaden horizons
through meeting new people,
traveling to different places
and doing new activities.
The year ended in a
Court of Awards and Bridging
ceremony, where 5 Cadette
girls bridged to Senior. The
girls spoke about the fun they
had learning new skills
together. This was a comfortable way for them to learn how
to do something and learn more about each other. They also
expressed their desire to continue to service the community,
so we will plan many more service opportunities next year.
This ceremony was a girl-run event that made all the parents
proud. It was a great ending to a great year!
Two girls earned the “From Dreams to Reality” patch. Thanks to all the parents for their wonderful support
This patch was a way to explore several aspects of many of their daughters and Troop 969!
different careers. The girls learned about how women balance
— Helen Shacter & Shirley Jernigan

===== PAGE 133 =====
Scouting
Cub Scout Pack 14
Cub Scout Pack 14 enjoyed a great year! We had
two camp outs and great participation from our Pack
Family. Pack 14 was seen camping at Echockotee and
Little Talbot. This years activities included hiking, learning
about whittling, playing mad libs and going on an alligator
scavenger hunt. They were also treated to a Pack 14-
style bonfire at Echockotee.
Our Pinewood Derby drew our pack’s families
together for a morning of racing competition and family
fun at the Center. We had some great award winning
designs.
Our dens learned about nature, safety, community
and Judaism. We are proud of our new den, the Tiger
Cubs. A big Scout salute to the first-grade Tiger Cub
Program. Tiger Cubs is geared towards boys in the first
grade as opposed to the traditional beginning of Cub
Scouting in the second grade. We congratulate our
WeBeLos who moved up to the Boy Scout Troop 14.
We are grateful to our den leaders: Mark Berlin,
Marty Pett, Garry Kitay, Robert Richter and Lisa
Wolfson and all our volunteer parents, who have
committed their valuable time to our children, the Cub
Scouts of Mighty Mighty Pack 14!
For information, call me at 739-2970.
— Cubmaster Bruce Goldring

===== PAGE 135 =====
Recreation
Camp Neshama
Camp Neshama was an amazing eight week
experience for all who participated. Campers and
staff came from all over - Jacksonville, Atlanta,
New York, South Florida, even Israel! We were pleased
to welcome many new campers along
with the “old-timers.”
From beginning to end, the
summer was filled with activities.
Swimming, Judaica, gardening,
music, arts & crafts, drama, sports,
computers and cooking were part of
the regular daily line-up. Tasty,
kosher lunches from Margo’s
Catering and snacks were a
highlight.
Specialty camps featured
horseback riding, wall climbing,
kayaking, cooking, ceramics, Tae
Kwan Do, tumbling and basketball.
Camp Neshama staged several big events -
a play, talent show, carnival, color wars and an
Israel day. Field trips included bowling and skating
as well as visits to the kitchen of 3
Sisters Chocolate, Jax NAS, Aqua
Zoo, Sprinkle’s Children’s Museum,
MetroPark, Marineland, Adventure
Landing and ice skating with the
Barracudas hockey team.
Of course, summer camp would
not be complete without sleepovers.
Dancing, swimming, pajama parties
and campfires added to the fun.
Thank you to a wonderful staff.
Rest up and get ready for another
exciting and funfilled summer at
Camp Neshama 2004.
— Pamela Maman, Camp Director

Now you can call or leave voice mail directly to the party or department you

your party is unavailable, you will be given an opportunity to leave a

located in the dominant markets of the Sunbelt region. Our centers are
positioned in high growth, urban markets that have experienced above
average growth rates for population, employment and per capita
retail sales. But for all our size, we make it a priority to build EQUITY
personal relationships with each of our tenants. Our on-site |
property management and maintenance teams are there to
answer and understand your day-to-day needs, so you don’t
have the headaches of dealing with a big bureaucracy.
And when you’re ready to diversify - either with new locations within
a state or into a new region - the relationship we’ve built will serve
us to find you further spaces in one or more of our many locations
throughout the Sunbelt
So come join The Supermarket REIT and benefit from our
many great locations, 20+ years of local expertise and friendlier
hassle free transactions.

Statistics show that 48.6% of people age 65 and over may spend some time
in a nursing home.1 But the truth is that most people, even when faced with
long-term care needs, would rather stay at home.
A long-term care insurance policy from John Hancock can help cover the
care you receive at home. It also covers care in an assisted living facility
or a nursing home. It’s nice to know that if you or your spouse ever had a
long-term illness or injury, you both would have the option to get the
care you need in a place where you’re more comfortable, familiar with
your surroundings, and close to your family and friends.
Find out more about an insurance policy that will help you stay at home.
1. Health Insurance Association of America, Long-Term Care: Knowing the Risk, Paying
the Price, 1997.
Mark Lodinger
& Associates
8834 Goodby’s Executive Drive • Jacksonville, FL 32217
Phone 737-9166 Fax 448-9578
CALL NOW FOR MORE INFORMATION 904-737-9166
Long-term care insurance policies are underwritten by John Hancock Life
Insurance Company, Boston, MA 02117. The Long-Term Care Insurance
policy describes coverages under the policy, exclusions and limitations,
what you must do to keep policy in force, and what would cause your
policy to be discontinued. Please contact the licensed representative or
John Hancock for more information, costs and complete details on coverage.

The Jacksonville Jewish Federation
serves as a central resource for our Jewish
community. In summary, the Federation is
dedicated to providing for the welfare of
every Jewish person living in Jacksonville.
Through a partnership with the United Jewish
Communities, formerly known as UJA, we
are equally committed to the survival of, and
quality of life for, every Jew living in Israel
and throughout the Diaspora.
The five major local recipient agencies
of funds raised by the Federation are the
Jewish Community Alliance, Jewish Family
& Community Services, River Garden
Hebrew Home, Jacksonville Jewish
Foundation and the Solomon Schechter Day
School. We are proud of the invaluable
services provided by these five outstanding
Jewish agencies. It is a privilege to assist
them in trying to meet their goals.
Jewish education is extremely
important, and the Federation is proud to
support the Solomon Schechter Day School,
Beit Midrash Hebrew High and Etz Chaim
Hebrew Academy. Through the Joan Levin
Gift of Israel program and birthright israel,
Federation is helping to make the dream of a
trip to Israel a reality for Jewish teens and
college youth in our community. All of the
synagogues in our community receive funding
from the Federation campaign.
The Federation is involved with
community relations, leadership development
and Missions to Israel. We will continue to
work in cooperation with our local agencies,
UJC and the synagogues to address the vital
issues and challenges in the entire arena of
Jewish continuity.
Last fall, Federation conducted a
demographic study of our Jewish Community.
The information we are receiving from this
study is going to serve us as we begin this fall
with a Long Range Strategic Planning Process
in cooperation with the synagogues and major
local agencies.
Our Officers and Board of Directors wish
the congregation a happy and healthy New Year.
— Dr. Guy Benrubi, President
Alan Margolies, Executive Director

Mission: To ensure the future of our Jewish community and life with dignity for every Jew.
To ensure that our synagogues and agencies have the financial resources they need so that
generations to come may enjoy our rich Jewish heritage and traditions.
Partnership: Beth El -The Beaches Synagogue, Beth Shalom Congregation, Congregation
Ahavath Chesed (The Temple), Etz Chaim Synagogue, Jacksonville Jewish Center,
Jacksonville Jewish Federation, Jewish Community Alliance, Jewish Family and Community
Services, River Garden Hebrew Home.
Summary: The Jacksonville Jewish Foundation is truly our Jewish community Foundation,
providing planned giving and endowment services to our partners in order to further the
stated mission.
B’nai Tzedek: B’nai Mitzvah youth are invited to establish their own B’nai Tzedek funds.
B’nai Tzedek.members participate directly through the Jacksonville Jewish Foundation
partnership in implementing a plan to perpetuate the future of the Jacksonville Jewish
community. Participants contribute $125 of their funds, the Jacksonville Jewish Foundation
contributes $250. B’nai Mitzvah youth take an active role in giving throughout this Jewish
community.
Book of Life: Imagine a time in the future when a child’s fingers touch a page in the
Foundation Book of Life... The questions begin... why is your name in the inscription in this
precious book of memories? An inscription in The Book of Life is a promise to establish an
Endowment Fund on behalf of any of the Jacksonville Jewish Foundation partners. Leave
your living legacy of caring for those in need... inscribe your story now.

Our Jewish identity is important. The JCA seeks to create a positive and affirming
environment of Jewish culture and heritage. We strive to welcome all and share our
Jewish traditions.
The mission of the JCA is to (1) contribute to the continuation of Jewish life,
culture, and community (2) provide a common meeting ground for the Jewish community
(3) enhance the quality of life for all segments of the community and (4) strengthen
family life. The JCA fulfills its mission through an integrated range of high quality
programs for people of all ages including: childcare and family programs, fitness and
recreational facilities and activities, Jewish education, culture and arts programs, and
by providing a place for family, “neighborhood,” and community gatherings.
The JCA takes pride in working with the Jacksonville Jewish Center and other
local synagogues and agencies in conducting special educational programs and
celebrations.
New classes and programs are always being added to meet the diverse interests of
our members. We serve the Jacksonville Jewish community with programs like the
NAEYC accredited Gan Yeladim preschool, after school care for elementary age youth,
the Challenge Program, Yiddish for Fun, adult Torah study group, classical music
appreciation, pottery classes, children’s birthday parties, computer classes, yoga, aerobics,
Middle School Night Out, Great Books discussion group, swim instruction, gymnastics,
swim team, tennis teams and clinics, aqua aerobics, youth, teen and men’s basketball
leagues, Mommy and Me program, Jacksonville Teens Volunteer program, Theatre of Youth,
summer camp accredited by the American Camping Association and so much more ...
The JCA serves people of all ages from 6 weeks to senior adults. We invite you to
be a part of the JCA. A sliding fee scale is available to make membership affordable to
all. Come by for a tour, or take part in one of our many programs - after all, YOU
ALREADY BELONG.
Shalom!
River Garden Auxiliary
The River Garden Auxiliary began in 1922 with a small group of
ladies who called themselves the Ladies Hebrew Home Sheltering Aid
Society. The group was formed to help care for residents in the home
on Riverside Avenue. Although as an organization we have grown, our
goals remain the same, to enhance the daily lives of each and every resident.
Our volunteers are an ever-present part of the Home, fulfilling the
needs of our residents with love, a smile, and a tender touch. Their
volunteer time to the Home and residents is given unselfishly and with
a dedication that is unwavering. The Auxiliary also provides financial
support for ancillary needs and services for the residents.
As part of the Auxiliary, you can make a difference. Join us in our
commitment to “Honor thy father and thy mother.”

Community Agencies
River Garden
HEBREW HOME/WOLFSON HEALTH & AGING CENTER
11401 Old St. Augustine Road • 260-1818 • www.rivergarden.org
A Gold Seal Community
“Honor thy father and mother that thy days may be long . . .” It was this
commandment which inspired the founding of River Garden Hebrew Home in
1946. It was this commandment which nourished the love and care that for more
than fifty years has made River Garden a nationally recognized model of excellence
in its field. It was this commandment that made it necessary to create a Home that
is welcoming to families and encourages its use as an extension of family space.
River Garden residents are a part of the community, not apart from it!
The River Garden Hebrew Home has also become the anchor of a growing
system of elder services including the Home, The Coves, Family Care Support
program and Home Health Agency. The success of River Garden is based on the
tradition of meeting 100 percent of local Jewish community needs and of serving
rich and poor alike with excellence. The River Garden Foundation accepts
donations to help River Garden continue to meet its mission. This would not be
possible without substantial charitable support from the community and the work
of The River Garden Foundation to stimulate planned gift annuities, trusts and
bequests.
River Garden’s programs of short-term rehabilitative/respite care, long¬
term residential care, Alzheimer’s/Adult Day Care and outpatient therapies serve
hundreds of people a day. These programs are guided by a devoted, professional
full time staff of over 230. Staff includes physicians and beauticians, nurses,
social workers, pharmacists, activities specialists, physical occupational and
speech therapists, dieticians, etc. In addition, scores of dedicated volunteers help
create a special caring community.
Located on a 35 acre Mandarin campus containing lush Florida oak and
pine trees, a private lake, meandering walking paths, River Garden is the perfect
setting for residents and visitors. River Garden is a community where people
live, love and care. It is a community of many lifestyles and of rich Jewish content,
and a community which every day strives to live up to the mandate of the Fifth
Commandment.
River Garden
foundation
The River Garden Foundation is a philanthropic organization, established
to provide resources for programs and facilities to enhance the quality of life for
the aged. Its primary purpose is to fund the not-for-profit River Garden system of
services.
The foundation is dedicated to helping the elderly remain in control of their
own lives by assuring services to people at all levels of need and financial ability.
The aim of the Foundation is to keep pace with the changing needs of the
aging through programs that meet a broad array of health care needs, as well as
provide a full spectrum of residential options.
This elegant yet affordable
retirement community is located on
River Garden’s 35 acre campus in
Mandarin.
Sponsored by the not-for-profit
River Garden Holding Company, The
Coves offers comfort, security,
clubhouse living and the opportunity for
continued growth during the retirement
years, in a Jewishly sponsored
environment.

Jewish Family & Community Services
6261 Dupont Station Court East
Jacksonville, FL 32217 • Phone 448-1933
Iris T. Young, Executive Director
Mount Carmel
Gardens, Inc.
5846 Mt. Carmel Terrace
Jacksonville, FI. 32216
(904) 733-6696
The mission of Jewish Family & Community Services
is to strengthen the entire community by providing
vital family and individual services to anyone, without
precondition or prejudice, in a manner rooted in the
Jewish tradition of helping people to help themselves. In
the coming year, JFCS will continue to serve seniors,
families, couples, individuals, children and those in need.
Some of the many services offered by JFCS:
Adopt-A-Senior
You can help support Kosher Nutrition, and the elderly
in our community who rely on the program, by
“adopting” a senior. Call 448-1933 to learn more.
Adoption
JFCS continues to place babies into loving homes
across the country, including Florida, Connecticut and
New York, three states that require a license to place
children.
Bus Rental
Now the community can rent the JFCS buses to shuttle
guests to and from life cycle events and family gatherings.
Enjoy bar and bat mitzvahs, weddings and other special
occasions without the headache of coordinating rides for
out-of-town guests.
Community Kosher Nutrition Program
CKNP continues to provide hot, nutritious, kosher meals
to the elderly at Mt. Carmel, in a safe and friendly environment.
Counseling
JFCS provides quality mental health care by licensed professionals, at reasonable
rates. Confidentiality is always guaranteed. Services include counseling for grief,
depression, family issues, parent-child conflict, life transitions and much more.
Emergency Financial Assistance
JFCS provides past due rent and utilities, FEMA assistance and SHIP dollars for
deposits to the needy in our community. Confidentiality is always guaranteed for
all services. Information and referral services are also available.
Feed A Needy Neighbor
With donations of non-perishable food items from a concerned community, JFCS
provides emergency groceries to families and individuals experiencing difficult times.
Jewish Healing Network
The Jewish Healing Network reaches out to those who are struggling, ill or dying
by sharing the rich resources within the Jewish tradition.
Jewish Hospice Connection
JFCS collaborates with Community Hospice Northeast to offer services to Jewish
individuals. When a member of the Jewish community enters the hospice program,
a social worker from JFCS will be assigned. If requested, a volunteer from the
Jewish Healing Network will be provided, as well.
Senior Transportation
JFCS transports seniors to religious services, doctors appointments, shopping centers
and recreational activities for an affordable fee.
There’s So Much More ...
These are just a few of the many services offered at JFCS. For those needs the
agency cannot address, staff is alway available to refer you to the appropriate resource.

American Red Magen David for Israel
Founded in 1930 as a First Aid Society, Magen David
Adorn evolved into Israel’s emergency medical, disaster,
ambulance and healthcare network - 24/7. Every person in
every corner of Israel looks to MDA to perform the usual
tasks carried out by Red Cross Societies throughout the world,
and then some. You are undoubtedly familiar with MDA in
action, having viewed on TV our white and red ambulances
rushing to the scene of the latest terrorist attack. You’ve also
witnessed MDA’s medics, paramedics, drivers and volunteers
working at to save countless lives. The unrelenting atrocities
have placed a heavy toll MDA resources.
Mitzvah Chapter’s Annual Raffle and Annual Concert
proceeds this year will be used to purchase depleted medical
equipment and supplies for the Hadera-Eiron Region. If you
would like to make a contribution to this fund, please send a
check to Mitzvah ARMDI, 4485 Rock River Road W.,
Jacksonville FL 32224.
Though the symbol of Magen David Adorn, a Red Star
of David, is recognized by the American Red Cross, and the
International Red Cross has finally acknowledged there is a
problem, efforts are still going on to achieve international
acceptance of our symbol. Support for the State of Israel with
a membership of only $25 or $200 Chapter Life and do the
mitzvah of pikkuach nefesh by joining today. Mail to Mitzvah
ARMDI, 9830 Woodrose Lane, Jacksonville, FL 32257
For us it's only a check, for them it could mean life
itself
Brandéis University
National Women’s Committee
Brandéis University Women’s Committee is really a
misnomer, since our organization has many men, as you will
note from our officer’s list. Our primary goal is financial
support for Brandéis University and its Libraries, as well as
supporting scholarship funding. It connects Brandéis, a
nonsectarian university founded by the American Jewish
Community, to its members and their communities through
programs that reflect the ideals of social justice and academic
excellence.
Brandéis - Jacksonville covers a diverse range of
interests. Our Study Groups offer something for everyone,
from reading books and plays to great dining and more.
Our membership includes couples as well as singles
(women and men). We afford our members the opportunity to
continue learning, as well as the chance to just have fun.
“Traveling Gourmet” features dinners at various area
restaurants with emphasis on the exotic. “Reel Special,” our
movie group, picks films of unusual interest, followed by
dinner and discussion. “Food for Thought” is the strength of
such groups as “Great Literature,” “Current Events,” as well
as many other offerings.
We welcome everyone to join with us in this unique
organization. If you would like additional information, please
contact our Membership Vice President, Estelle Kritz at 636-
6636 or President, Norma Levy at 641-7335.

Hadassah
National Council of Jewish Women
“Hadassah has always been an important bridge to
peace. By treating all people without regard to nationality
or religion, Hadassah has shown the world what peace in
the Middle East will look like.”
— Yitzchak Rabin, 1994.
The National Council of Jewish Women (NCJW) is
a volunteer organization, inspired by Jewish values, that
works through a program of research, education, advocacy,
and community service to improve the quality of life for
women, children and families, and strives to ensure
individual rights and freedoms for all.
Judaism teaches that it is not enough to avoid iniquity,
we must actively pursue righteousness and justice at home,
in the community, and in the world. In this tradition,
Hadassah was founded in 1912 by Henrietta Szold to bring
public health services to pre-state Israel. Today, more than
300,000 American women support our network of Israel
projects in addition to our volunteer work at home. Across
the US, Hadassah promotes health education, community
service, and Jewish education and research. Hadassah
advocates on issues ranging from Israel-US relations to
First Amendment protections to women’s rights and health
concerns.
One by one, we must each take responsibility for
transforming hopes, promises, and echoes into deeds.
Jacksonville Hadassah invites your participation in one of
our five groups: Hannah Senesch, Shir Li, Tikva, Nurse’s
& HCP Council and Yamit.
For information please contact
any of our Presidents:

The Jacksonville section of NCJW was established
in 1939, and is currently involved in such programs as:
1. Organizing forums for candidates for local offices to
present their views to the Jewish community;
2. Bringing the CARGO gun safety program to
Jacksonville;
3. Bringing kosher meals, as well as a caring word, to
homebound Jewish people;
4. Organizing advocacy on state and federal issues
involving women, children, and families;
5. Encouraging Jewish participation in the interracial
Study Circles project.
6. Providing a Hanukkah celebration at Wolfson
Children’s hospital, bringing entertainment and gifts to
patients;
7. Registering voters, as part of a national “Promote the
Vote” campaign;
8. Providing entertainment and refreshments to Mt.
Carmel residents;
9. Recognizing women who have made great
contributions to our community, through our annual
Women in Power luncheon;
10. Helping seniors to overcome isolation through the use
of computers; and
11. Continued support of programs which we helped start,
and which now function independently, such as Guardian
ad Litem, Home Instruction Program for Preschool
Youngsters, and PACE.
For information, contact Gloria Einstein.

Jacksonville Mitzvah Clown Corps
Forming a Mitzvah Clown corps at the Center was conceived
by Neil Maiman (at right), as a Bar Mitzvah project. With help
from his parents, Leonardo & Lynn Maiman, Neils idea
blossomed. We express our gratitude to them for bringing this
valuable program to our community.
Amid laughter and a sea of bright colors, fifty Mitzvah
Clowns were “bom” at the Jacksonville Jewish Center in April
2002. The group participated in the inaugural Mitzvah Clown
training session conducted by “Buttercup,” “Sweet Pea” and
“All Ears,” longtime Mitzvah Clowns affiliated with
Congregation B’nai Israel in Millburn, New Jersey and
supported by Danny Siegel’s Ziv Tzedakah Fund. The Mitzvah
Clowns seek to bring smiles and companionship to sick and
aged people while enhancing self-confidence from the joy of
performing mitzvot.
On the first day of training, twenty adults learned
clowning skills and methods of incorporating these skills in
furthering acts of kindness and community service. The next
day, 28 students from Solomon Schechter Middle School and
the Center Religious School’s Etgar class also learned how to
apply clown makeup, perform balloon sculpting and other
skills necessary to become a Mitzvah Clown. The two-day
event culminated in a visit with the residents of Mount Carmel
who greeted the Mitzvah Clowns enthusiastically as they
joined the Mitzvah Clowns in song and dance.
Our new Mitzvah Clowns have been busy since their
initial training: the SSDS 8th graders paid a visit to Wolfson
Children’s Hospital; the SSDS 7th graders visited Mt.
Herman Exceptional Student Center and other Mitzvah
Clowns entertained our children at this month’s Lag B’omer
picnic.
Plans are in the works for additional site visitations as
well as a fall training session. If you are interested in
becoming a Mitzvah Clown, please send a postcard with
your name, address, phone number and e-mail address to
Mitzvah Clowns c/o of the Jacksonville Jewish Center.
